Ministry of Communications Restricts Airline Free Tickets 135

Even Travel on Official Business Should Be Reported Quarterly

The Ministry of Communications, considering that the operating income of the China Eurasia Aviation Corporation is insufficient to cover expenses and urgently needs remedies, has increased postal rates to offset the deficit. It has also issued a circular: "In order to comply with the order, the company's aircraft have few seats, and free tickets should not be issued in the future. Even service personnel of the company, from the general manager down, should not travel arbitrarily unless necessary for official business. From this year, all personnel traveling on free tickets for official business should list their names, travel times, departure and arrival locations, and submit them quarterly for verification."

1932 Jiangsu Province Agricultural Production Harvest Statistics 136

Increased Harvest Compared to the Previous Year

According to the East China News Agency, the Department of Agriculture of Jinling University reports that the national agricultural harvest in the past year was better than the previous year (i.e., 1931), with an increase of about 25%. This is because the previous year was affected by floods. However, the wheat crop was the second worst in the last five or six years. Overall, the quantity of various harvests last year was more abundant than in the most recent five or six years. As of the end of November of last year, over 1,000 reports had been received from various provinces regarding the national harvest statistics for last year. A total of 129 reports were received from 41 counties in Jiangsu Province. The harvest quantities for last year and the previous year are recorded below: (1932) [The following are in units of one dan]: Wheat 5.837, Barley 3.231, Rapeseed 58, Early Rice 4.019, Late Rice 4.654, Soybeans 2.684, Corn 625, Sorghum 1.084, Sugarcane 4.065, Cotton 345. (1931) Wheat 6.061, Barley 3.267, Rapeseed 59, Early Rice 2.873, Late Rice 3.54, Soybeans 2.141, Corn 547, Sorghum 857, Sugarcane 3.175, Cotton 274. (The above are all major agricultural products).

US-China Negotiations on Continued Loan of American Wheat Suspended 137

US Side Dissatisfied with Guarantees Offered

US Representative Remains in Shanghai to Seek Alternative Solutions

According to the Shanghai News Agency, negotiations on the continued loan of American wheat from the US Financial Rehabilitation Corporation have been suspended because the US side is dissatisfied with the guarantees offered by the Chinese side. However, the US representative stationed in Shanghai is still working hard to find new solutions to avoid a breakdown. Details are provided below:

Stumbling Block for Suspension: It is widely rumored that the biggest stumbling block to the suspension of the continued loan of American wheat is the opposition of the national public. However, according to the Shanghai News Agency reporter's investigation, when the Ministry of Finance began negotiations with the US Financial Rehabilitation Corporation, national public organizations sent telegrams of opposition. Finance Minister Song Ziwen even issued a statement on this matter, stating that the continued loan of American wheat would not harm the national food problem. It is clear that the Ministry of Finance's sudden suspension of contact with the US side was not due to public opposition, but because the US Financial Rehabilitation Corporation was dissatisfied with the guarantees offered by the Chinese side for the continued loan of American wheat. The Chinese side was also unwilling to continue due to the harsh conditions of the US side, leading to the abrupt suspension of negotiations between the two sides. The US representative stationed in Shanghai has reportedly telegraphed the authorities, reporting the process of the suspension of negotiations.

US Representative Remains in Shanghai: Another report states that the US Financial Rehabilitation Corporation recently telegraphed its representative stationed in Shanghai, instructing him to continue negotiations with the Chinese Ministry of Finance regarding the continued loan of American wheat and to consider the guarantees offered by the Chinese side in order to avoid a breakdown. Therefore, the US representative is currently planning to find new solutions in the hope of breaking the deadlock.

Song to Return to Nanjing Tonight: Finance Minister Song Ziwen's purpose in coming to Shanghai this time was to contact the Shanghai banking community to discuss financial issues. After several days of meetings, the result was very satisfactory. The US Financial Rehabilitation Corporation's representative stationed in Shanghai even visited Song some days ago to discuss the continued loan of American wheat. However, due to various reasons, Song expressed his unwillingness to continue negotiations, resulting in no results. It is learned that Song has completed his official business in Shanghai, and the central government in Nanjing has many affairs awaiting his approval. Therefore, he has decided to return to Nanjing by night train tonight.

No Such Thing as Rice Being Shipped to Japan 138

Reports that the Japanese side is secretly purchasing white rice in Shanghai for export to Japan and Dalian are surprising. According to responsible personnel of the Customs Administration, the export of white rice from this port has always been prohibited. However, since the bumper harvest this autumn, rice has been stockpiling on the market, and the price of rice has been falling. Therefore, since December 24th of last year, the Jiangsu Provincial Government has allowed merchants to obtain passports to transport rice out of the province, but only to various domestic ports (excluding the three northeastern provinces). It is heard that the largest quantities of this white rice are shipped to Tianjin, Yantai, and Qingdao. As for shipping to Japan and Dalian, there is absolutely no such thing.

Meeting Minutes of the Bean and Rice Trade Association 139

The Shanghai Bean and Rice Trade Association held a joint meeting of the northern and southern market traders at Cuixiu Hall in the city at 2:00 PM yesterday. Committee members present included Zhu Zixiang, Yan Xiaoquan, Chen Yuming, Chen Ziyi, Cai Yukun, Zhu Xiangsheng, Jiang Zisheng, Zhu Ziming, Wang Shengyuan, and over a hundred people. Because Chairman Gu Xinyi had other important business, Chen Ziyi was elected as temporary chairman, and the meeting proceeded as usual. The following resolutions were passed: (1) To determine how to reduce the rice price when new measuring instruments are implemented on February 1st. Resolved: When using the new municipal bushel, each stone of rice will be calculated at 85% of the sea bushel market price at the time of the great settlement. (2) To reply to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce's inquiry about the precedent for distributing public reserve funds to stores. Resolved: To reply as previously agreed. (3) To re-investigate the names of various colleagues. Resolved: To do so in the future, once every year. (4) To reply to the Shanghai South distributor's inquiry about the names of the shareholders of Wan Kangxing. Resolved: To have the Shanghai South branch office investigate and reply. (5) The Social Affairs Bureau issued instructions that, based on the request of the Anhui Rice Industry Association in Shanghai for Anhui rice to be shipped to Shanghai, it should be reported whether the rice from the lower reaches of the river is lightly measured. Resolved: Anhui rice shipped to Shanghai has always been measured in level bushels and is no different from the rice from the lower reaches of the river. Since the Anhui rice industry has objections, it is possible to change the measurement to weight in the future, with each stone calculated as 200 pounds. Report this to the Social Affairs Bureau. (6) Procedures for new businesses to join this association. Resolved: In the future, when new colleagues join this association, they must have a member of this association recommend them and consider them qualified before they can be registered, issued a membership certificate, and licensed to operate. The meeting adjourned at 5:00 PM.

Ministry of Military Affairs Prohibits Soldiers from Forcibly Boarding Freight Cars 146

The Ministry of Military Affairs issued a notice yesterday, posted at various stations along the Beijing-Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo railway lines, regarding the following matter: The Railway Police Administration Bureau of the Ministry of Railways reported that soldiers from the Independent Brigade of the Fourth Division stationed in Fengyang County forcibly boarded freight cars at Mentai Zi Station every time they went to Bengbu. Despite repeated polite dissuasion, the soldiers ignored it and even sought trouble and beat railway staff. A letter was sent to the Fourth Division requesting strict prohibition to emphasize the importance of freight cars. The headquarters of the division replied, stating that the brigade commander had been ordered to strictly prohibit subordinates from forcibly boarding freight cars again and to send personnel to Mentai Zi Station to strictly arrest and punish offenders.

In view of this, it is found that responsible transportation has been gradually implemented on all routes. The responsibility for guarding freight cars is extremely important. No personnel should forcibly board freight cars during transportation. The Transportation Regulations clearly stipulate this. However, the garrison troops along various routes are unaware of this and often forcibly board freight cars as they pass by, refusing to be dissuaded and even deliberately making trouble for the railway police, delaying traffic. Such a situation hinders the future of railway transportation. It is appropriate to consult and order the commanding officers of the garrison troops along each route to strictly prohibit this and issue and print notices to be posted at various railway stations to maintain railway administration. It is hereby ordered that responsible transportation has been gradually implemented on all routes. No military personnel shall forcibly board freight cars to maintain the railway. In accordance with the previous consultation, in addition to issuing a circular to the garrison troops along each route to strictly prohibit their subordinates, a public notice is hereby issued for general knowledge. You must strictly abide by this notice. Minister He Yingqin.

The Shanghai Charity Relief Association for Disaster Areas in Henan, Hubei, and Anhui received an official letter yesterday from Kang Jiyao, Chairman of the Shaanxi Provincial Relief Association, stating: "With respect, the disaster in Shaanxi has continued for years and is now increasingly severe. Previously, when your association was in charge of raising relief funds for the three provinces of Henan, Anhui, and Hubei, we earnestly requested that Shaanxi be included, not to distribute the funds already raised, but only to allocate some of the relief funds raised in Shanghai and other places in the future to Shaanxi to help those in need. Recently, the Executive Yuan decided to allocate 500,000 yuan to Shaanxi, Henan, Hubei, and Anhui, although the funds have not yet been delivered. This shows that Shaanxi, like Henan, Hubei, and Anhui, is one of the provinces most severely affected by the disaster and should be treated equally. We earnestly request that Shaanxi be formally included to extend compassion and relief. We will be eternally grateful."

The Ordeal of Wang Sibao, a Child Without a Father 153

His Mother Sues Wang Qiduo in Court

Seeking Confirmation of Paternal Relationship

Wang Qiduo, residing at No. 18 South Wuxi Road, met Bu Huiying, a woman from Wuxi, in the 18th year of the Republic [1929]. At the time, the woman was 39 years old. Initially, their relationship was covert, but by the first month of the following year, they were formally cohabitating. They originally hoped to spend their lives together, but after only ten months, they separated. On the 22nd day of the eleventh month of that year, Ms. Bu suddenly gave birth to a baby boy, who is now three years old. According to Ms. Bu, the child was conceived during her cohabitation with Wang and should be Wang's son. Therefore, she gave him the surname Wang and named him Sibao. She contacted Wang to request support. Because Wang denied paternity, she has now retained lawyers Yan Jiangyi, Wu Saitai, and others to file a complaint against Wang in the First Special District Court. The plaintiff is the three-year-old child Wang Sibao, with Bu Huiying acting as his legal guardian. The lawsuit seeks confirmation of the father-son relationship. The complaint states that the plaintiff's mother, Bu Huiying, had a relationship with the defendant in the 18th year of the Republic [1929], and formally cohabitated in the first month of the following year, resulting in conception. In the tenth month of the same year, they ended their cohabitation. On the 22nd day of the eleventh month (i.e., the 3rd day of the tenth lunar month), the plaintiff was born. The birth of the plaintiff occurred just over one month after the separation of his parents. The conception clearly occurred during the period of cohabitation of the parents, leaving no doubt that the plaintiff is the defendant's son. The father-son relationship is based on blood ties. Although the relationship between the parents has ended, its effect cannot extend to their offspring. The defendant intends to abandon the child, leaving the plaintiff as a child without a father. Previous requests to the court for mediation were unsuccessful. Therefore, it is necessary to file this complaint with the court, requesting confirmation that the plaintiff is the defendant's son, and that the defendant be ordered to bear the costs of the lawsuit. This would be a virtuous act. The First Special Court recently held a hearing, summoning both parties for interrogation, but the proceedings have not concluded and will require further hearings at a later date.

The Commercial Press Commemorates the Anniversary of the Destruction of its Main Factory 154

—Business as Usual on January 28th—

—Employees Donate Salaries for Relief—

The anniversary of the January 28th Incident, which also marks the anniversary of the destruction of the Commercial Press's Zhabei main factory by Japanese troops, was commemorated with the publishing department operating as usual, and the plate-making, printing, and lithography departments continuing their work as normal to demonstrate a spirit of perseverance. At 8:15 AM, a memorial ceremony for the destruction of the main factory was held in the publishing department's store, with all staff from the general management and publishing departments in attendance. General Manager Wang Yunwu delivered a speech, outlining a three-point review of the past year, the significance of the struggle, and future directions for that struggle. Employees from various factories and warehouses, due to the distance, could not all attend, but they stopped work for five minutes starting at 8:15 AM. The company's employees also voluntarily initiated a one-day salary donation to support the National Aviation Defense Movement.

In other news, to commemorate the victims of the January 28th Incident, the Commercial Press is offering all new books published daily from January 28th to February 3rd at half price. The deadline for purchases in Shanghai is February 11th, and for mail orders from other locations, the deadline is February 28th. From January 28th to February 11th, a National Goods School Supplies Exhibition will be held, showcasing the latest physics equipment, chemistry equipment, specimen models, sports equipment, music equipment, scouting equipment, surveying instruments, and educational toys manufactured by the company. The completeness of the range and the excellence of the manufacturing surpass the company's products before the disaster, demonstrating significant progress. Many educators visited the exhibition and expressed deep appreciation for the rapid recovery of the Commercial Press's various operations.

Dr. Euwe Wins 40 out of 47 Games

To Continue Playing Ten Games Tonight Blindfolded

Dr. Max Euwe, the world-renowned chess grandmaster, showcased his skills yesterday at the YMCA gymnasium. ｜Gamblers Always Lose｜

French Detective Li Aicai (transliteration), Chinese Detectives Li Yousheng, Deputy Detective Liu Kunbao, Detectives Bao Zhaolin, Dai Rongji, Bai Xiumei, Zhang Wenliang, etc., discovered that someone had set up a deceptive rolling game at No. 48 Baoyu Lane, Caishi Street, which the perpetrators referred to as "slaughtering the pig," meaning that gamblers always lose. Hair Salon Owner Shot and Killed 160

｜Two Thugs Commit Heinous Act Out of Grudge｜

At 5:35 AM the previous morning, just as dawn was breaking, two thugs speaking with a Jiangbei accent suddenly barged into the hair salon of Lu Lian'gen, located at No. 219 Yaoshui Lane, Xiaoshadu, West Shanghai. One was wearing a blue cloth overcoat, and the other was wearing a dark-colored long robe. They entered directly, making a ruckus, and demanding to see "Old Lu." Seeing that the situation was not good, the owner's wife, Lu Mao, replied that he was not there. The two thugs stood still for a moment, then said they wanted to collect a debt from her. They turned to leave, but unexpectedly, about ten minutes later, the two thugs rushed back in again. One of them pulled out a pistol and fired a shot at Lu Mao, hitting her in the chest. She collapsed to the ground in agony, bleeding profusely. Seeing that their goal had been achieved, the two thugs turned and left, firing two shots into the air as a warning before fleeing. The owner of the shop, Lu Lian'gen, immediately reported the incident to the local Sixth District Police Station, which then reported it to the General Administration. The injured woman was rushed to Baolong Hospital for treatment, but unfortunately, due to the severity of her injuries, she died shortly after. The Sixth District ordered the local district head to report to the District Court for an inquest. Subsequently, the court-appointed prosecutor arrived at the scene and determined that the victim had died as a result of being shot in a vital area. The family was instructed to prepare the body for burial and await the apprehension of the murderers for severe punishment. It is rumored that the reason for the shooting was a grudge against Lu, prompting the thugs to commit this heinous act of revenge.

Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce Writes to Public Utilities Bureau Requesting Rectification of Jiangwan Bus Services 163

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce wrote to the Municipal Public Utilities Bureau yesterday, stating: "Respectfully, on the 23rd of this month, we received a letter from the Jiangwan Branch Office of the Chamber, stating that various businesses have complained about the corrupt management of the Chinese Public Bus Company and requested the Public Utilities Bureau to strictly reform it. The complaints are summarized as follows: (1) Unlimited passengers, endangering public safety. The company's vehicles have signs at the entrance stating that the car is limited to 28 passengers. Although clearly stipulated by the Public Utilities Bureau, the cars are often loaded with 50 or 60 people, with greed as a common occurrence. Passengers who want to reach their destination are unable to squeeze off the car. How can it not create opportunities for thieves to pickpocket? (2) Ticket checkers, ticket sellers, and drivers are mostly impolite, arrogant like noble princes, looking down on everyone, scolding and fighting as common practice. Even military officers do not issue orders to their subordinates in such a tone. There are often women in the area who sell wool, carrying goods in front and back, occupying seats every day, and these people arbitrarily approve or reject the boarding of old women and young girls. How can public utility personnel be so corrupt? (3) Using inferior engine oil, harming public health. When the vehicle starts, there is an indescribable stench that emanates from the front of the vehicle and spreads to the rear, filling the cabin. People on opposite sides cannot distinguish each other's faces. How can it be tolerated when the north wind is severe and the doors are tightly closed? The above three points are the corrupt situation of the company. Public utilities are closely related to the development of the city. At the beginning of Shanghai's public utilities, all our citizens should warmly support it. To supervise improvement is our inescapable duty. Since the operation of this vehicle, it has provided much convenience to merchants and villagers in the area. However, the company is only interested in profit, ignoring the purpose of public utilities, and using the patent right as the only protection, without concern for corruption. The local needs are like this, and the corruption of the company is like that. The harm to the city and the citizens is increasing day by day. The competent authorities should not tolerate it. Although it is said that the losses from this war were not small, the simplification should not reach this extreme. This matter has been presented to Supervisor Jiang by the local Party Headquarters. It has not changed in a month. Therefore, we re-emphasize the recent situation and request that the Municipal Public Utilities Bureau be promptly forwarded for realistic training and reform. It will not only be the fortune of Jiangwan, but also the future of the city. Based on this, the public bus service in this city was originally intended to develop the city and facilitate public transportation, and the operation should strive for perfection. According to the statements made by the branch office, all passengers on public buses believe that the statements are true and that strict rectification is urgently needed. Accordingly, we hereby send this letter, hoping that your Bureau will investigate and promptly order the company to strengthen the improvement, so as to benefit passengers and so on."

International Propaganda Society to Lecture on International Issues 164

Saturday Evening

The Chinese International Propaganda Society, in order to awaken the nation and pay attention to international affairs, and to work together to overcome national difficulties, has decided to hold a lecture on international issues at the Yongsheng Company Radio Station on Nanjing Road from 7:00 PM to 8:00 PM on Saturday evening. The society has invited famous speakers, including Liu Zhankai, Gui Zhongfu, Liu Dajun, Lin Yutang, Yang Xingfo, Guo Bingwen, Gong Zhibin, Wang Xiaoying, and others, to lecture in rotation every week. The lecture topics are divided into two groups: (Group 1) Major International Issues of the Present Time: (1) The Attitudes of the Great Powers Towards the Lytton Report, (2) The Relationship Between the United States and the Philippines, (3) The Prediction of the Consequences of Japanese Militarism, (4) The Cause and Effect of the Arms Race Between the United States and Japan, (5) The United States' Attempt at War Debts and Disarmament, (6) The Trend of Germany's Demand for Equal Military Preparation, (7) France's Attitude Towards Germany in the Past and Present, (8) Italy's Work in the Last Ten Years and the Future, (9) The Impact of the Success of the Soviet Union's First Five-Year Plan, (10) The Indian National Movement; (Group 2) International and China: (1) The Loss of the Northeast and the Awareness that the People Should Have, (2) The Way to Recover Lost Territory, (3) The Attitude that China Should Take Towards the International Community Now, (4) The Way that China Should Take Before Military Preparations are Completed, (5) Methods to Expand the People's Vision, (6) The Preparations that the People Should Have During the National Crisis, (7) The Preparations that the Government Should Have During the National Crisis, (8) The Steps to Take to Recover Concessions, (9) China's Role in the Occurrence of a Second World War, (10) China's Critical Moment of Life and Death. The lecturers will choose their own topics from the above or set their own, which will be announced again. After the new year, the society will hold a large-scale public lecture again in a larger venue. In addition, the society will form an international affairs lecture team to travel to various provinces and regions to lecture. The group is currently being organized. In order to gather the strength of the Chinese people, the society has formulated a charter to solicit members in seven categories. Those who wish to join the society can contact the society for a brochure.

Six Boat Collisions on Huangpu River 165

Near the end of the year and the beginning of spring, there have been six boat collisions on the Huangpu River, which can be described as eventful. The circumstances of the incidents are recorded separately below.

Xin Ningxing Damages Wooden Boat: A stone boat of Zhang Hexing Shipyard in this city, which was carrying crushed stone on the morning of the 18th of this month at the No. 2 Wharf of Dafeng, Nanshi, was hit and sunk by the Rongji ferry. The shipyard then sent another Ningbo-style wharf to salvage the sunken boat. At 8:00 AM on the 24th, while the boatmen were working, the Xin Ningxing, a ship of the Sanbei Company, which was berthed at the Ningbo-Shaoxing Wharf to the north, turned away from the shore and headed south, damaging the stern wood of the wharf boat and breaking the lead rope, resulting in a loss of over one hundred yuan. Afterwards, the boat owner, Zhang Aru, reported the incident to the Maritime Customs Water Patrol Police for investigation.

Jinghu Ferryboat Sinks Passenger Ferry: At 9:50 PM on the 24th, the No. 1 passenger ferry of the Pujiang Ferry Company on Jiujiang Road, with eight passengers on board and driven by Xia Yuxiang, set off from the company's wharf and headed towards the Dongjiadu Shipyard outside the Pudong river. At that time, the Customs Jinghu ferry, sailing from south to north at high speed, suddenly collided head-on with the passenger ferry. The small ferry could not withstand the impact and tilted, taking on water, and gradually sank to the bottom of the river. All eleven passengers and crew members were rescued by the Jinghu ferry crew, which was fortunate.

Xin Ning Shao Sinks Coal Boat: At 5:00 AM on the 25th, a coal boat owned by Wang Linfu, carrying 25 tons of coal, sailed to the Ning Shao Wharf at the 16th Pier and moored, preparing to unload it onto the Shanghai-Ningbo route Xin Ning Shao ship. Before long, the ship arrived at the port, and when it was turning to berth at the pier, the propeller in the back suddenly struck the front section and starboard side of the coal boat, creating two holes. Water immediately poured in, and the entire boat sank to the bottom of the river, fortunately without causing any injuries.

Baohe Wheel Damages Stone Boat: At 10:20 AM on the 25th, two stone boats, No. 12325 and 23435, owned by Chen Daoyou, were moored on the Pudong Lujiazui riverfront outside a barge belonging to the Huangpu Engineering Bureau, unloading cargo. At that time, the Jardine Matheson & Co.'s Baohe steamship was sailing from downstream and turned at that location, simultaneously damaging both boats. Afterwards, the owner of the damaged boat, Weng Achun, reported the loss of 4,000 yuan to the Water Patrol Police for compensation.

Coal Boat Sinks Feces Boat: At 12:00 noon on the 27th, a feces boat owned by Wang Bingfu, carrying a full load of human waste, was moored on the Suzhou Creek near the Zhejiang Road Bridge. At that time, the Puan Company's No. 10782 coal boat entered the river from the Huangpu River during high tide. When it reached under the Zhejiang Road Bridge, it was suddenly hit by a small ferry belonging to the Huangpu Engineering Bureau. The steam boat was simultaneously pushed and collided with the feces boat, damaging the stern of the feces boat, which took on water and sank, filling the river surface with overflowing waste, which was unbearably foul.

Xin Su Wheel Damages Wheat Boat: At 12:50 PM on the 28th, a wharf boat owned by Yao Changgen, carrying 230 bags of wheat, sailed into the Suzhou Creek during high tide. Just as it reached under the Tianhou Palace Bridge, the Xin Su ferry behind it was also sailing in. Unable to avoid it, the Xin Su ferry struck the starboard side of the wheat boat, causing the wheat boat to collide with a tugboat on the south bank. The bow of the wheat boat was immediately damaged. Afterwards, Yao reported the incident to the Water Patrol Police for investigation.

Shipping and Customs Declaration Industry Pays 100,000 Yuan in Security Deposit 166

The Shanghai shipping and customs declaration industry, since the Ministry of Finance Customs Administration ordered Jianghai Customs Taxation Department Director Luo to strictly crack down on it, each household must pay a huge amount of security deposit in order to prove that the business firm has assets. It has been more than a year since the promulgation of the policy. The reason why it was not implemented in the past was that the capital sizes of the industry firms were different, but the amount of the security deposit was non-negotiable. Although the chairman and committee members of the industry, Shi Zhikun and You Senting, repeatedly consulted with Luo Taxation Department Director Fude to change the methods, the industry association raised 100,000 yuan to the Central Bank as a security deposit for all members of the association. In addition, those who have not joined the association will be cracked down on. On the 18th of this month, Luo Taxation Department Director was invited to a banquet at the Navigation Administration Club, and the difficulties of the industry were explained in detail. Luo Taxation Department Director was understanding. It is now heard that if the industry wants to do business, it must first apply to the association for membership, and only after the association has passed the examination and ordered the payment of a security deposit of 3,000 yuan can it do business.

Lu Jinfu Missing 167

Lu Jinfu, a native of Baitong, 21 years old, from a certain number on Dingxing Road behind Datong Lane, South Ke Road, is working as a messenger at a lawyer's office. There are still parents in the family. In the past, after finishing his service at the lawyer's office, he returned home. But on New Year's Eve, he walked out of his home late at night. It has been a few days since then, but he is missing. At first, Lu's parents suspected that he was working at the lawyer's office, but a lawyer said that Lu did not come to rest during the New Year. It was not until yesterday that they learned that Lu had been missing for many days. In addition to sending people out to investigate his whereabouts, they also reported to the local police station to inquire whether there were any vehicle accidents during these days.

Fire brigades from various districts arrived to extinguish the fire. Three houses, Nos. 526 and 528, were destroyed.

Reader's Consultant

Ambition and Inferiority 172

|| Cai Niansun's Letter ||

Yuan Daofeng said in "New Year's Dreams": "China will have a dictator in the future. If this dictatorship does not adopt the imperial system of Napoleon, it must adopt the republican form of Kemal. As for the form of Mussolini, he is unwilling to adopt it. This is because Chinese people have this inferiority complex, that is, they do not want a monarch superior to themselves." || See the New Year's issue of Oriental Magazine || Yesterday, I read the history lectures on the opposition and evolution of the Northern and Southern Dynasties, and I increasingly believe that Mr. Yuan's words are correct. Wasn't the usurpation of Jin by Liu Song, the usurpation of Song by Qi, the usurpation of Qi by Liang, and the usurpation of Liang by Chen, as well as the usurpation of Wei by Northern Zhou and Northern Qi, all because they were unwilling to have a monarch superior to themselves, so they wanted to replace them to satisfy the desire for "sole dominance"? In a certain sense, that kind of desire can be regarded as ambition. But the root of the problem also lies in this: personal ambition hinders the upward momentum of the nation and society! Here, I have two points to ask the reporter for guidance: ㈠ How is this kind of ambition (?) cultivated? ㈡ Why doesn't it exist in other ethnic groups? Please enlighten me!

Answer: The letter is confusing. I thought you were a middle school student, and I was very disappointed. I was unwilling to answer, but at the end, I saw that the place where the letter was forwarded was a pawnshop, and I thought you might be an apprentice, which is not surprising. Therefore, I will point out the errors in your letter one by one as follows. ㈠ Mr. Yuan Daofeng's high-sounding theories published in the Oriental Magazine have no basis at all. The so-called "dictator" in Western languages ​​is Dictator or Diktatur, which means dictatorship. Dictatorship is a form of state power. For example, the Soviet Union adopts the form of proletarian dictatorship, and democratic countries in Europe and America, such as the United States, Taiwan, Britain, France, Switzerland, and Germany, are all forms of bourgeois democracy dictatorship. The National Party governments of Italy and Turkey are forms of bourgeois one-party dictatorship (Mussolini and Kemal are just their representatives.) Some people say that China's current political form is similar to the dictatorship of the Turkish National Party, and there is no need for Mr. Yuan to come and hope or predict any "future". However, we will not study for the time being whether the political form of the Fascist Party or the Turkish National Party itself is good or bad. However, the Turkish National Party has made Turkey stand tall as an independent Eastern country. Although the Italian Fascist Party is also the extreme right force in capitalist countries, it can still maintain national independence. What about our country? We should not criticize "Chinese people" who "do not want a monarch superior to themselves" as our "inferiority complex". Before discussing whether this statement is correct, please ask Mr. Yuan to go back and study history before speaking. You must know that Mussolini and Kemal are not monarchs. The former's position is equivalent to the long-term prime minister, and there is still a monarch above him. The latter is the president of a republic. What "monarch" are you talking about? Because you read history, you "increasingly believe that Mr. Yuan's words are correct." The so-called "usurpation of Jin by Liu Song... and the usurpation of Wei by Northern Zhou and Northern Qi" are all "because they were unwilling to have a monarch superior to themselves, so they wanted to replace them to satisfy the desire for 'sole dominance'." This statement is even more specious. Because the opposition between the Northern and Southern Dynasties each had its material conditions and political background. All the disasters of "sole dominance" that followed the usurpation at that time were formed by the social system and autocratic history at that time. That is to say, this kind of political tragedy and evil psychology were the products of the social system and the history of autocratic politics at that time. It is the result, not the cause. You were shocked by Mr. Yuan's fallacies in the Oriental Magazine, so you inevitably reversed cause and effect and suffered a lot! As for the term "ambition," it has been completely misunderstood by people. If a person has gained some knowledge and has gained a little false reputation, but he is not satisfied with this, but feels that his reputation does not match reality and feels deeply ashamed, so he works harder and strives for perfection. This is ambition. A person leads troops to defend the territory. Although he knows that he will be defeated in the face of enemy planes and artillery, he still fights back with weapons and has no regrets even if he dies. This is ambition. An apprentice is unwilling to be insulted and abused by others, so he studies hard and struggles for the poor compatriots, disregarding his own interests. This is also ambition. The so-called "ambition" is to strive to be superior, not to be an emperor, to "be the first to worry about the world's worries and the last to enjoy the world's joys," not to have the ambition of "I am fat and the world is thin," to "treat the people as my brothers and sisters, and things as my companions," rather than to think about eating delicacies and owning billions of assets, to be the servant of all people rather than the running dog of one person and one family. Otherwise, that is a complete "inferiority complex"! To be honest, if you change your words and say, "㈠ How is this kind of ambition cultivated? ㈡ Why do other ethnic groups have it, but our ethnic group does not?" then we can have a good discussion, although it is still only smelling a part of the truth? If you are not satisfied with the above answer, please write to me and I will talk to you.

Record of the First and Second Days of the Chinese Education Society 174

Discussion on the Reform of Chinese Education

Request the Government to Limit the Elimination of Illiteracy Nationwide

| Election of Directors and Discussion of Articles of Association Today |

Since Liu Zhanen, Chen Heqin, Zheng Xigu, and others initiated the preparation of the Chinese Education Society, it has been several months. Education experts from various places have enthusiastically joined. The inaugural meeting was held at the YMCA in Baxianqiao from the day before yesterday to today. More than one hundred members from various places attended. The Central Party Department sent Yang Shulin, Secretary of the People's Movement Committee, and the Ministry of Education sent Shen Pengfei, Director of Higher Education, to attend the meeting and deliver instructions. The meeting discussed the reform plan of Chinese education and other experimental reports for several days. The agenda will be discussed today, and directors will be elected. The details are as follows:

Attending Members: Huang Jianzhong, Luo Jun, Gao Junshan, Fan Zhengkang, Gu Shusen, Chen Binhe, Zhang Zhonghuan, Hao Yaodong, Chang Daozhi, Wu Nanxuan, Xiao Chengzhen, Zeng Zuozhong, Ni Wenya, He Bingsong, Liu Manen, Yang Lianggong, Zhao Mian, Chen Lihong, Chen Zhaoheng, Wei Que, Mao Beiping, Xu Benzhen, Ou Yuanhuai, Zhao Yan, Zheng Ruogu, Li Haoshan, Zheng Xiaocang, Xie Xunchu, Shang Zhongyi, Liu Tingfang, Zhong Daozan, Shen Fuzhai, Liao Maoru, Li Qingsong, Ma Ketan, Xia Chengfeng, Shen Zishan, Tai Shuangchu, Chen Heqin, Cao Chu, Luo Tingguang, Dong Renjian, Yang Bao Kang, Zhang Yousan, Zheng Xigu, Mao Yanwen, Chen Kemei, Shen Yizhen, Yang Hengyu, Jiang Wenyu, Meng Huicheng, Zhang Shiyi, Zhu Ruoyi, Xiong Zirong, Qian Weizong, Wang Diancun, Xiao Xiaorong, Shen Sizhuang, Shu Xincheng, etc., more than one hundred people. Yang Donglin, representative of the Central Government, Shen Pengfei, representative of the Ministry of Education, and Pan Gongzhan, Director of the Shanghai Education Bureau.

Meeting Staff: The Presidium was nominated by the Preparatory Committee with Liu Zhanen, Jiang Menglin, Yang Lianggong, Zheng Xiaocang, and Luo Tingguang as members. Recorders were Shen Yizhen and Zhang Zhongnang.

㈠ First Day of Meeting 175

Opening Ceremony: The opening ceremony was held on the 9th floor of the YMCA at 9:00 a.m. ㈠ Perform the ceremony as usual. ㈡ Observe a moment of silence for the anniversary of the martyrs of the January 28th Incident. ㈢ Chairman's report. ㈣ Report of the Preparatory Committee. ㈤ Instruction from the representative of the Central Party Department. ㈥ Instruction from the representative of the Ministry of Education. ㈦ Instruction from the Director of the Shanghai Education Bureau. ㈧ Speech. ㈨ Photography.

Summary of Speeches: ㈠ Chairman Liu Zhanen described the purpose of the association and the significance of holding the meeting on January 28th. ㈡ Zheng Xigu, representative of the Preparatory Committee, reported on the organization's motives and preparations. ㈢ Yang Donglin, Secretary of the People's Movement Committee and representative of the Central Party Department, said that the only way to save the country from disaster is education, and he especially hoped that the association would contribute more to education during the national crisis. ㈣ Shen Pengfei, Director of Higher Education and representative of the Ministry of Education, hoped that the association would study practical problems that adapt to the environment. ㈤ Pan Gongzhan, Director of the Shanghai Education Bureau and representative of the Shanghai Municipal Government, hoped that the association would have a concrete and practical education reform plan and methods for promoting compulsory education for the administrative authorities to adopt. ㈥ Member Gu Shusen hoped that the association would contribute more opinions on ordinary education and normal education. He later stated that there was no conflict between child-centered education and nationalist education, and proposed that the association should promote the education community to advocate the purchase of airplanes.

Afternoon Meeting: The meeting continued at 2:00 p.m. with Yang Lianggong as chairman. First, Zhao Mian reported on the experimental situation of the Jiangsushengli Education Institute's North Xia Popular Education and Mass Education Zone (in Dongting, Wuxi). He described in detail the social background and facilities of the area, and gave a very detailed explanation of political education and economic education. Next, the Chinese education reform plan was discussed. First, Zhang Yousan reported on the report of the League of Nations Education Investigation Group. The summary of the content is divided into: ㈠ Basic principles, ㈡ Advantages, ㈢ Disadvantages, and ㈣ Points to be noted. Next, Huang Jingen reported on two major issues in modern Chinese education: ㈠ The problem of popularization, ㈡ The problem of improvement, and the points to be noted in elementary and secondary school enrollment, and the points that the association should strive for. Shao Shuangchu reported on the movement of people's livelihood education, and elaborated on the meaning of life and education and people's livelihood education, and the implementation methods of people's livelihood education in detail. Liu Tingfang, Shang Zhongyi, Shu Xincheng, Wei Que, Huang Jianzhong, Ou Yuanhuai, Zheng Xigu, Que Shuangqiu, Luo Tingguang, Xie Xunchu, and others successively expressed many opinions on the basic principles of the report of the League of Nations Education Investigation Group. The meeting adjourned at 6:00 p.m.

㈡ Second Day of Meeting 176

Third Meeting: The meeting continued at 9:00 a.m. yesterday with Shao Xiaocang as chairman. First, Zheng Xigu, Principal of Shanghai Middle School, reported on the actual experience of the Huangdu Rural Normal School of Engineering. Next, the reform plan of higher education was discussed. Huang Renjian introduced the case report and summarized the opinions of everyone. The meeting adjourned at 12:00 p.m.

Afternoon Session: The session continued at 2:00 p.m. with Luo Tingguang as chairman. First, Jiang Wenyu, Director-General of the China Vocational Education Society, reported on the society's experimental experience in the Xu Gongqiao Education Experimental Zone. Next, the reform plan of secondary education was discussed. Liao Shicheng introduced the report and summarized the opinions. The motions were: ㈠ Vocational subjects should be set up in popular secondary schools. ㈡ The new secondary school curriculum standards promulgated by the Ministry of Education are not practical. It is recommended that the Ministry of Education allow public and private secondary schools that conduct overall planning experiments to make adjustments and start investigating and collecting statistics on the difficulties encountered after implementation. ㈢ Secondary school education and its teacher training institutions should pay attention to education methods and the goals of secondary education. Jiang Wenyu, Zheng Xiaocang, Zheng Xigu, Xu Shoulian, and others all spoke extensively.

Discussion of Association Affairs: After the discussion of secondary education issues was completed, the articles of association were discussed according to the agenda. More than 50 members present made a joint temporary motion to advance the discussion: ㈠ The association should always maintain the spirit of academic research to conform to the purpose of initiating the association (resolution passed). ㈡ Since the association is based on academic research, the qualifications of members should be strictly defined (resolution passed in principle). When discussing Chapter 3 on members of the articles of association, a concrete decision was made. ㈢ In order for members from other places to actively participate in the association's affairs, the directors of the association should be elected by district (resolution passed). Before the election, the membership list should be printed by district so that the election will not be biased in one area. The discussion ended at 5:45 p.m. and the meeting was adjourned.

㈢ Today's Agenda 177

Scheduled Motions: The meeting will continue at 9:00 a.m. today with Liu Zhanen as chairman to discuss the association's articles of association, elect officers, and discuss association affairs: ㈠ Where should the next session be held? ㈡ Determine the location of the association and its fund. ㈢ Prepare for publications. ㈣ Request the Academia Sinica to establish an education research institute. ㈤ Request the China Education and Culture Foundation to subsidize education research. ㈥ Request the government to stipulate an absolute deadline for eliminating illiteracy nationwide. In the afternoon, topics on normal education and elementary education will be discussed, followed by the opening ceremony. Tonight, various academic groups in the city will hold a public banquet at the Xin Xin Restaurant.

Shanghai Defeated Hong Kong 3 to 2 in the Interport Football Match 183

= Corlett Scored the Winning Goal in the Last Minute =

= Shanghai Lost to Hong Kong Chinese United | 5 to 2 =

= Tam Kong-pak, Fung King-cheung, and Ip Pak-wah Showed Great Prowess =

Victory over Hong Kong Interport 184

| 3 to 2 |

(Hong Kong, 26th) The 1932-33 Shanghai-Hong Kong Interport Football Match was held at the Happy Valley Stadium here this afternoon. More than 10,000 Chinese and Western spectators attended. As a result, the Shanghai team defeated the Hong Kong team 3 to 2. The Shanghai team's scorers were Corlett (2 goals) and Chen Jiaqiu (1 goal). The Hong Kong team's scorers were Da Gaoshan Nu and Ran Zhaozhao (1 goal each). The Shanghai center-back line was very strong, especially Fan Ensi, who was outstanding.

Shanghai Lineup

Braley, Feng Yunyou, Turner, Fan Ensi, Za Xu, Remy D Hughes, Chen Jiaqiu, Corlett, Jack, Ke Zhi

Hong Kong Lineup

Lo Cha, Liu Mao, Alan, Duncan, Pai Duo, Ran Rongzhao, Si Lu, Xiao Gaoshan Nu, Da Gaoshan Nu, Huang Meishun, Zheng Shaokang

Hong Kong Scored in the First Minute: The Hong Kong team kicked off first and had the advantage of the wind, so they took the offensive. The Shanghai team tried hard to resist, but after just one minute, Da Gaoshan Nu went straight in and scored a goal. The Shanghai team's army was unlucky, and the defense showed panic at times. Fortunately, left-winger Ke Zhi attacked along the edge, and Chen Jiaqiu also seized the opportunity. However, Hong Kong goalkeeper Lo Cha calmly saved them all. Ke Zhi once had a perfect opportunity, but unfortunately, the ball rebounded from the goalpost. Corlett also frequently tried to shoot, but none of them hit. Later, Hong Kong defender Alan missed his footing, and Corlett got the opportunity to shoot, but his strength was weak and Lo Cha saved it. Corlett shot again fiercely when the ball rebounded, and the goalkeeper could not save it, making it 1 to 1.

Shanghai Took the Lead 2 to 1: Shanghai left-forward Jack, seeing Corlett's success, also wanted to work hard, but he performed too much individually, so although the opportunity was good, none of them hit. Then, Chen Jiaqiu got the ball, dribbled past Pai Duo, and shot from the 20-yard mark. It was accurate and rapid, and Lo Cha could not save it. The ball went into the net again. In the first half, the Shanghai team took the lead 2 to 1.

Liang Rongzhao Scored and Lost: After the lemon time, the Hong Kong team was eager to counterattack and attacked the goal very quickly. Then, Ke Zhi injured his foot, and Shanghai fought with ten players. Hong Kong's offensive became more intense. Later, Ke Zhi returned to the field, and the momentum turned strong. Unexpectedly, Feng Yunyou missed his footing, which was almost dangerous. Ten minutes before the end of the game, Fan Ensi of Shanghai fouled outside the penalty area. Liang Rongzhao took the penalty, and the ball went into the goal from the right corner, making it 2 to 2. At this time, both sides attacked fiercely, and the back and forth was rapid, which was very exciting. Unexpectedly, Feng Yunyou suddenly fouled in the penalty area. This ball was quite suspicious, so Liang Rongzhao kicked it intentionally wide of the goal and made it a wild ball, which won applause from the whole audience.

Corlett Made the Final Contribution: At this time, the Shanghai team's position was quite dangerous because Chen Jiaqiu suddenly reported a foot injury. Fortunately, he entered the field soon. In the last minute, Corlett finally scored a goal to decide the outcome. As a result, the Shanghai team won 3 to 2. Looking at the overall situation, Shanghai's connection was excellent, and center-back Fan Ensi was the most outstanding. The defense was weaker, and goalkeeper Braley seemed to be better than Lo Cha that day. The Hong Kong center-back line, except for Liang Rongzhao, was average.

Lost to Chinese United 185

| 2 to 5 |

(Hong Kong, 28th) The Shanghai Interport Football Team, which defeated the Hong Kong Interport Team 3-2 on Thursday, lost to the Hong Kong Chinese United Team 2-5 this afternoon. The Shanghai team's representatives remained unchanged except for Hughes replacing Remy D. The number of spectators reached 17,000, a new record for this season.

Shanghai Team Lineup

Braley, Lu Yunyou, Turner, Fan Ensi, Za Xu, Hughes, Chen Jiaqiu, Corlett, Jack, Ke Zhi

Hong Kong Chinese United Team Lineup

Lin Tiancan, Liu Mao, Li Tiansheng, Deng Guang, Lin Yuying, Liang Rongzhao, Chen Guangyao, Ip Pak-wah, Fung King-cheung, Tam Kong-pak, Zheng Shaokang

The Chinese United Team Had Strong Strength: In the first half, the Hong Kong Chinese United Team took the lead with 1 to 0. Their strength was indeed strong. Although the Chinese United Team increased by four goals in the second half, if the Shanghai team had good luck, they could have hit at least four goals. The scorers for the Hong Kong Chinese United Team were Tam Kong-pak and Fung King-cheung (2 goals each), and Ip Pak-wah (1 goal). The scorers for the Shanghai team were Chen Jiaqiu (1 goal) and Corlett (1 goal).

The First Half Ended 1-0: In the first half, the Chinese United Team took the offensive mostly. One minute after the kick-off, Ip Pak-wah had a shooting opportunity, but it did not hit. The Shanghai team counterattacked, and the Chinese United defender kicked it out. Fung King-cheung sent the ball to both wings with great certainty. Shanghai goalkeeper Braley tackled a dangerous ball kicked by Zheng Shaokang and collided with Ip Pak-wah. He was injured and left the field. He returned after a few minutes. Then, Tam Kong-pak received a warning for tripping Za Xu. Za Xu wanted to raise his foot to shoot, but seeing Ke Zhi on the side, he passed the ball to Ke. Unfortunately, this ball went wide. Corlett also had several opportunities, but he did not shoot immediately after passing to both wings, so he lost a good opportunity. Tam Kong-pak got the ball from Fung King-cheung, dribbled past Yi Na, and scored with one foot at the goal. In the first half, Hong Kong Chinese United 1, Shanghai 0.

Fung King-cheung Also Scored: The second half continued. Jack lost an opportunity to hit an empty goal. Za Xu passed the ball very accurately. Corlett once broke into the hinterland of the Chinese United team, but the shot turned into a wild ball. Ke Zhi was very active. His shots made Lin Tiancan unable to catch them, and he also unfortunately hit the crossbar, twice. All did not succeed. At this time, the Shanghai team took the offensive entirely, but the Chinese United team took advantage of the situation and returned to score. It can be said that the Shanghai team lost countless opportunities. When Hughes was flustered, Fung King-cheung scored another goal for the Chinese United team.

Corlett Recaptured a Goal: The Shanghai team failed to score repeatedly and lost another goal, which can be said to be extremely unfortunate. However, the momentum of pressing on the Chinese United team did not diminish because of this. After repeated efforts, center Corlett also established a credit for Shanghai. The Chinese United goalkeeper was now the target of public criticism. Corlett got the pass from Hughes and hit the vital point.

Chen Jiaqiu Headed in One: Tam Kong-pak then shot in with a swift foot, and Chen Jiaqiu of the Shanghai team also got a clever cross from Ke Zhi and headed it in. At this time, the score was Chinese United 3, Shanghai 2. The tension of the situation was unprecedented. The audience shouted and became even more enthusiastic, which was rare in Hong Kong football matches.

5 to 2 Chinese United Won a Big Victory: The last two goals were scored in five minutes. Hughes got the pass from Jack and was only three yards away from the goal and could have kicked it in to tie the game. However, Hughes failed to take advantage of this great opportunity, which led to a slump. When everyone was in a melee in front of the Shanghai team's goal, Braley was injured in the head and left the field for a few minutes before returning. Then, a fire broke out in the stands, and the audience's attention was shifted, and then it was extinguished. The Shanghai team then launched a major offensive. Hughes took a long shot that almost hit. The Chinese United team counterattacked, and Fung King-cheung got the pass from Ip Pak-wah and shot in a goal, and Ip also shot in from 30 yards. The Hong Kong Chinese United team won the final victory with a score of 5 to 2.

The Pirate Team has strong strength and a great reputation in Shanghai. All the Chinese and Western teams in Shanghai are inferior to them and dare not show off. People at the time said that the King from beyond the pass overwhelmed the pirates on the sea. Five Games Overview 191

The Military Academy came to Shanghai and fought five games in a row. In the first game, they lost to Shanghai University 46 to 63, due to bad luck and the fouling out of two forwards. In the second game, they gradually revealed their true skills, and each of the five tigers made contributions, winning against John 48 to 28. Everyone embraced the determination to fight to the death, calmly responding to the battle. In the five-man defense, they adopted the method of individual surveillance, both internally and externally, and finally won 30 to 24.

Once they return to school, there will be a grand welcome. Du Tingxi, the leader of the team, said that there are very few strong enemies in Beijing. In the future, they will work harder and live up to the expectations of the Chinese people. It is expected that in the whole army competition, the Military Academy team can compete with the national talents.

Finance 193

Post-Holiday Gold Market Review

···Rebounded by 5.4 Taels···

Although Silver Price Rose, Gold Price Rebounded 194

On the eve of the Lunar New Year holiday, the gold market trended upwards again, mainly because the international situation was volatile. Although US silver rose by 0.625, bank telegraphic transfers only increased by 0.375. The measures taken by the industry were not appropriate, and the exchange rate was tightened first and then loosened. The banks' appetite was originally healthy, but it became increasingly tight, so the gold market saw a rebound. Initially, overseas silver markets in London rose by 0.1875 across both spot and forward contracts, and US silver rose by 0.625. Forward silver prices also rose by more than 0.04. Both the British pound/US dollar and US dollar/British pound exchange rates continued to surge. Although the opening price was low at 774.5 taels, down 3.1 taels from the previous close, because bank telegraphic transfers did not rise much, stocks also fell slightly. The exchange market opened without any significant easing, and market sentiment was still good. Shunli initially offered to sell at 774 taels, Qian Changxiang came in and increased to 5 taels, and Daxingyong also increased to 6 taels. Shunli retreated to 5.5 taels. Citibank bought US dollars for April delivery at 0.9375, and Changshengyong advanced to around 6 taels. January sterling traded at 0.375. HSBC wanted to settle, and Hengmei went on the market to buy, pushing it up to 7 taels, and there was a period of consolidation. As for April US dollars, they only traded at 0.8125, which was 0.125 tighter than the initial opening, so there was an increase. Hengxing and Dadecheng competed to buy, and in a blink of an eye, it rose to 79.9 taels. After selling some goods, it went downstream again, hovering around 9 taels. When Sumitomo bought sterling for April delivery at 0.3125, there were no transactions in the market, and it jumped to 81 taels. Finally, because the price was raised too sharply, sellers became active, and it fell back by about 2 taels to 79.7 taels. The trading volume was light. Dadecheng continued to buy at around 80 taels, and Hengxing bought aggressively, and the exchange market was also tight. MacCarry bought US dollars for April delivery at 0.8125, and it rose to 81.7 taels and consolidated. HSBC announced that the sterling rate was flat and the US dollar rate rose by 0.025. Hengyu initially offered to sell, retreating to around 80 taels, plus 0.0875. US dollars for May delivery could not be sold. Qingfayong continued to sell at 78.8 taels. Afterwards, there were not many transactions, and it was often seen hovering. Later, news came that the Central Bank opened 280 telegraphic transfers, and finally pulled up. Wanxing, Shunli, and Yuanchun all bought, and Dadecheng and others also bought telegraphic transfers as agents for the Central Bank's opening of spot transactions, and broke through 80 taels again. Afterwards, the industry replenished exchange, and the gold price did not go downstream, but it also fluctuated for a while. Yuanchun continuously cleared short positions, although the amount was not large, it was able to hold the price at around 80 taels. Yingfeng and Henglai bought at 0.03 taels, and Ruikang retreated to 79.5 taels. Cuichang advanced to 0.05 taels. US dollars for April delivery traded at 0.0875, and US dollars for February delivery traded at 0.0625. Mitsui blocked all bids, and it fell to within 80 taels. Dadecheng and Wanxing bought again (the Central Bank's spot price was 80 taels). Yuanmaoyong bought telegraphic transfers, and general retail investors all came to raise the price to 2 taels. Yuanchun also advanced to 82.6 taels. Datong sold US dollars for January delivery at 0.05625, and it dropped to 0.05 taels. Afterwards, because the exchange market was tighter than the previous day's closing, and the Central Bank's price was expected to shrink, market sentiment turned better. The Dalian gang, Wanxing, advanced again to 83 taels. The transaction price only turned back a bit. The final result was still 783 taels, an increase of 5.4 taels compared to the previous close. It was found that although the city only traded for half a day, there was a fluctuation of 9 taels. In addition, due to the Lunar New Year holiday, the trading volume was slightly narrow. The highest price was 783 taels, and the lowest price was 774 taels. February registration was 785 taels, March registration was 783 taels, and water replenishment was 783 taels. There was no real transaction in arbitrage, but in fact it was still generally an increase of 10.05 taels.

Fewer Price Quotations and Less Trading 195

The price quotation was because the US dollar exchange rate announced by HSBC rose by 0.025, and the gold price was 849.56 taels, a reduction of 66 taels, a decrease of about 13 taels compared to the previous close (on the 4th). There were fewer trades among industry players. Hengxing, Dadecheng, Changshengyong, Qian Changxiang, Cuichang, Yuanmaoyong, Wanxing, and spot brokers all bought, while Shunli, Qingfayong, Hengyu, and Ruikang sold. Yuanchun gradually covered short positions, accumulating small amounts into large sums. In addition, there were few trades and no fixed trend.

Overnight Interest Rate at the End of the Settlement Period 196

Estimate of Silver Dollars Shipped to Dalian Last Winter

January 25th was the Lunar New Year's Eve in our tradition, and it was also the last day of the general settlement for the commercial sector. All annual business procedures must be completed on this day, and the silver money industry is no exception. Therefore, the amount of collection and settlement procedures is also the most complicated of the whole year. It is estimated that the total amount of collection and settlement by foreign banks reached 45 million, while the collection and settlement by Chinese banks was also 67 million. Foreign merchants deposited 2.2 million into warehouses, and Chinese merchants deposited 1.2 million. The collection and settlement of money houses and silver brokers was more than 60 million, and the collection and settlement of foreign public companies was more than 20 million. The market price of foreign taels in the morning market was 7 qian 1 fen 2 li 2 hao 5 si, and in the afternoon market it was 7 qian 1 fen 2 li 7 hao 5 si. The transaction volume was 1.825 million in the morning market and 840,000 in the afternoon market. The bill of exchange volume was 65,000 in the morning market and 70,000 in the afternoon market. There were no transactions in banknotes in either market. Because the transaction of overnight interest rate bills had ended, there was no market to open, so there were no quotes in either the morning or afternoon market. The Jiangnan small silver dollar was 6 qian 0.08 li in the morning market and 6 qian 0.02 fen in the afternoon market, with a difference of 1 fen 0.01 li between the two markets. The transaction volume was 7,500 jiao in the morning market and 15,000 jiao in the afternoon market. The Guangdong small silver dollar was 5 qian 9 fen 5 li in the morning market and the same price in the afternoon market. The transaction volume was 135,000 jiao in the morning market and 35,000 jiao in the afternoon market. The silver dollar increased by 5,000 wen, to 405,000 wen. The transaction volume was more than 49,800 strings.

Last winter, silver dollars were transported north to Dalian and transferred to various parts of the three northeastern provinces, which caused a stir in society. In fact, it was not surprising, but a normal state of trade. However, under the control of the Japanese, this kind of attention was paid. According to investigations, the amount exported to Dalian was no less than 30 million yuan during the winter. A certain British shipping company carried approximately 23 to 24 million yuan. There were great benefits to transporting and selling the silver coins. With the Shanghai silver tael falling, it was not difficult to profit from it. Over the years, 10 to 20 million have been transported out, but without the means to do so, and the majority of those transported were those of the 3rd year of the Republic.

A Review of the Yarn and Cotton Market Over the Past Year (3) 199

Cotton Market Conditions also peaked in the spring, at which time the old exchange transactions were settled and cleared together with cotton yarn, while there was still activity in spot cotton trading outside, because the yarn factories in the concession still had operations, but the Japanese yarn factories completely ceased operations. However, due to the impact of the incident, transportation on all routes was blocked, and sources of supply withered, so cotton prices suddenly became sharp. The spot price of Shaanxi cotton reached a maximum of thirty-five taels, and American cotton also reached 7.2 cents. After the war ceased and the Japanese army withdrew, American and Indian cotton, which had previously been transshipped, were successively re-shipped to Shanghai. The exchange also reopened for bidding on cotton on May 2nd. Because the standard for cotton yarn was changed to 20-count "Ren Zhong" yarn, the cotton standard was also changed to Zhengzhou fine staple cotton. On the opening day, the price was 32 taels. By mid-June, due to sluggish sales of American cotton, inventories reached 13,449,900 bales. The Ministry of Agriculture and Commerce had 1.3 million bales of cotton in storage, and sold half of it, causing the market to plummet and reach an unprecedented low (falling to 5 US cents per pound upon entry). Shanghai was also in a state of financial contraction after the Japanese army's great robbery, yarn prices fell sharply, and yarn factories were shut down for as long as three or four months. The outlet for cotton turned sluggish again. Once the weakness was exposed, violent fluctuations followed one after another. Last year (1932), there were major floods in various provinces, and cotton merchants were deeply concerned that cotton production would be affected, so they ordered a large amount of foreign cotton. When it arrived, there was a lot of accumulated stock, and there was no intention to import more domestic cotton. As a result, the prices of Lu and Yu cotton all fell sharply. The inventory in Tianjin was very large, and the price of Xihe cotton fell even more severely. The financial sector suffered losses, and many cotton merchants went bankrupt. Bad news came frequently from all directions, and short sellers became increasingly active. The state of panic in the market was indescribable. At the same time, a major crisis occurred at the Ningbo Yao Cotton Exchange. There were only sell orders and no buy orders at the opening. For a time, the situation was deadlocked. With the intervention of the authorities, the cotton was temporarily accepted and efforts were made to sell it in Shanghai. As the saying goes, "when it rains, it pours." In July, the lowest record in recent years was found in the bidding for cotton: 27 taels (converted to 25.2 taels using the old standard). Just when things were at their worst, news suddenly came from overseas that American cotton fields had been damaged due to climate change, excessive rainfall, and increasingly serious insect infestations. A surge in prices suddenly occurred. On August 8, the US government estimated that the crop would be one million bales less than expected, at 11.306 million bales, a jump of 85 points. The price soared from 6 cents to 9.2 cents, approaching the 10-cent mark. The highest price for standard cotton in Shanghai reached 35.7 taels. A certain manufacturer made a large number of sales in the futures and spot markets, with a short position of 230,000 to 240,000 dan, accounting for two-thirds of the market, putting especially heavy pressure on prices. Unexpectedly, the second estimate of American cotton (announced on September 8) plummeted by more than 100 points. The world cotton market was shaken and fell sharply, like a bolt from the blue. The price of standard cotton fell by 1.7 or 1.8 taels. American cotton then slowly declined. The reason for the sharp decline was that the weather improved, production gradually increased, and the economies of Europe and the United States were sluggish, reducing consumption. In the last period, December 8, production increased to 12,727,000 bales, and the spot price fell directly from 9.2 cents in August to 5.7 cents in early December. The cotton market in Shanghai was completely shattered. Liang cotton fell from 35.7 taels in August to 29.75 taels in early November. However, domestic cotton in November, due to the soaring gold price, found a new high price of more than 830 taels. It was not feasible to calculate the price of foreign cotton coming to Shanghai, and there was a shortage of goods arriving in Shanghai from all over the country. Speculative shops actively purchased cotton. Moreover, there was excessive rainfall in the north, and the Yellow River burst its banks, flooding the provinces of Hebei, Shandong, and Shanxi, causing heavy damage to cotton fields. Production was estimated to decrease from 10,829,162 dan to 8,094,863 dan. This was indeed the biggest reason for the rise in domestic cotton prices. Therefore, at the end of the year, the price of standard cotton reached 34.65 taels again. (Note 3) The price of standard cotton in January 1932 was based on 16-count yarn raw cotton coarse lint. From May onwards, it was changed to 20-count yarn as the standard. Therefore, standard cotton also included Zhengzhou fine staple cotton.

(Note 4) Items marked with × are recent (July) prices.

The spot cotton situation, although there was a rise in the spring due to insufficient supply, soon subsided due to sluggish yarn sales. Since entering the summer season, the new cotton situation has been good. There is a rumor that the factories in Shanghai have borrowed 500,000 bales of American cotton on credit. The yarn factories once convened a meeting, but it did not materialize due to conditional relationships. In the autumn, American cotton experienced a sharp rise due to insect infestations. Domestic cotton had a period of brisk sales. Huoji cotton rose from 27 taels in June to 33 taels in August. Shaanxi cotton rose from 27.5 taels to 35 taels. At that time, Japanese factories absorbed more than 100,000 dan of Huoji cotton futures at a price of about 34-35 taels. Chinese factories purchased less. Unexpectedly, the second estimate of American cotton brought about unexpected changes, and spot cotton trading suddenly became cold. 100,000 dan of Huoji cotton purchased by Japanese factories were valued at 32 taels, but the settlement was not accepted. The market suddenly had this large amount of spot goods. In October, the price of Huoji cotton fell back to 28.25 taels. At that time, the bullish and bearish sides in the exchange were fiercely competing. Wing On Factory decided to purchase and take delivery, while Shenxin bought spot and delivered goods. The delivery volume was 50,600 dan, which was the largest amount in a year.

In December, a sudden rise in the cotton market in Shanghai made the situation particularly tense, and there was talk of a squeeze. The reason for this was said to be that a certain factory had too large a short position and did not have the capacity to deliver enough goods. Moreover, the price of gold was trending upwards, and it was difficult to calculate the price of foreign cotton coming to Shanghai in silver. Domestic textiles had to purchase domestic cotton for use, and domestic cotton sales were bound to be less sluggish than in the previous year. This was the biggest boost to the cotton market. As a result, general speculators rushed to buy, and the market rose. Japanese merchants were particularly active in purchasing spot cotton in the market. The spot price of Shaanxi cotton rose from 31 taels to 33-34 taels. However, the world cotton industry was still in an era of oversupply. The total production of American cotton, including carryover from the previous year, was 26,176,000 bales, while the worldwide consumption was only about 12.5 to 13 million bales. China's production was better than last year (according to the China Cotton Production Improvement Association, it was estimated to be more than 8 million dan). China has more than 4 million spindles, and the annual consumption of raw cotton requires more than 8 or 9 million dan, which it can supply itself. Moreover, the yarn market is in a sluggish state, and factories purchase raw materials as they use them. Judging from the overall situation, there is still no active upward momentum in the future. The high and low prices of spot cotton transactions throughout the year are listed below for reference (the market was closed in February due to the Japanese invasion of Shanghai; unit: taels).

Foreign cotton imports date back decades, but at that time the quantity was small and the value was no more than ten thousand taels. In the late Guangxu period, with the development of the yarn factory business, foreign cotton imports also increased day by day. However, at that time, the people were simple and unadorned, and coarse cloth clothing was sufficient to satisfy their desires, and there was no need for fine staple cotton. Later, there was a growing demand for fine staple cotton, and the call for promoting American cotton became louder. However, due to political, personnel, climate, land, and other factors, more than 30 years have passed, and the results of improving cotton varieties are clear but insignificant. Habits have also become increasingly extravagant. In the past, coarse cloth clothing was considered sufficient, but now it is difficult to satisfy desires without fine cloth or mercerized cloth. As a result, the value of American cotton and other imports has been more than ten million taels since 1920. In 1931, due to the vigorous purchase of foreign cotton by various factories, the import value and foreign rice firmly ranked first. Even yarn and cotton had to be raised to the standard of 20-count yarn and fine staple cotton. A higher standard of living is not necessarily a bad thing, but seeking everything from abroad and the country's agricultural production are closely affected by foreign goods, unable to maintain their position. Whether it is rice or cotton, there is no exception. As a result, it seems that we will gain nothing and will have to rely on foreign countries. The national economy and the people's livelihood are only shrinking and not prosperous. Without war, we can already be subdued. The cotton prices in foreign cotton markets are listed below.
